The entry ticket for Indian adults is reasonably priced at ₹52, with different rates applicable for international tourists and students.         "text": {
          "text": "Sheesh Mahal (Mirror Palace) inside Amber Fort is truly a jewel of Jaipur’s royal heritage. The moment you step into this part of the fort, you’re greeted by a dazzling sight — walls and ceilings covered in thousands of tiny convex mirrors, intricate glass mosaics, and floral patterns inlaid with precious stones. Even a single candle or ray of sunlight transforms the whole hall into a shimmering galaxy of reflections.\n\nBuilt during the reign of Maharaja Man Singh in the 16th century and further enhanced by later rulers, Sheesh Mahal was used as a royal reception hall and private chamber for the queens. One of its most fascinating features is its ability to illuminate with minimal light — a single flame could create the effect of a starry night sky, allowing the royals to enjoy beauty and warmth without open flames.\n\nThe craftsmanship here is beyond words. Every mirror piece is hand-cut, and every floral motif is painted with natural colors, showing the unmatched skill of artisans from centuries ago. It’s not just architecture; it’s poetry in glass and stone.\n\nPhotography here is an absolute delight, but nothing compares to seeing it with your own eyes — the way light dances across the walls feels almost magical. The area is well-maintained, though due to preservation efforts, some parts are restricted for visitors, which is understandable given its delicate nature.\n\nIf you’re visiting Amber Fort, Sheesh Mahal is the heart of the experience. Take your time here, look closely at the details, and imagine the royal gatherings, music, and laughter that once filled this sparkling hall.\n\n⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐",

        "originalText": {
          "text": "Sheesh Mahal (Mirror Palace) inside Amber Fort is truly a jewel of Jaipur’s royal heritage. The moment you step into this part of the fort, you’re greeted by a dazzling sight — walls and ceilings covered in thousands of tiny convex mirrors, intricate glass mosaics, and floral patterns inlaid with precious stones. Even a single candle or ray of sunlight transforms the whole hall into a shimmering galaxy of reflections.\n\nBuilt during the reign of Maharaja Man Singh in the 16th century and further enhanced by later rulers, Sheesh Mahal was used as a royal reception hall and private chamber for the queens. One of its most fascinating features is its ability to illuminate with minimal light — a single flame could create the effect of a starry night sky, allowing the royals to enjoy beauty and warmth without open flames.\n\nThe craftsmanship here is beyond words. Every mirror piece is hand-cut, and every floral motif is painted with natural colors, showing the unmatched skill of artisans from centuries ago. It’s not just architecture; it’s poetry in glass and stone.\n\nPhotography here is an absolute delight, but nothing compares to seeing it with your own eyes — the way light dances across the walls feels almost magical. The area is well-maintained, though due to preservation efforts, some parts are restricted for visitors, which is understandable given its delicate nature.\n\nIf you’re visiting Amber Fort, Sheesh Mahal is the heart of the experience. Take your time here, look closely at the details, and imagine the royal gatherings, music, and laughter that once filled this sparkling hall.\n\n⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐",

Located near Sawai Mansingh Stadium and in front of the Vidhan Sabha road, this magnificent monument left a lasting impression on me.\n\nImpressive Architecture and Ambiance\n\nThe architecture of Amar Jawan Jyoti is a marvel, with a beautifully designed structure that exudes patriotism and pride. The continuously burning flame at the monument's center is a powerful symbol of the sacrifices made by our brave soldiers. The surrounding greenery adds to the serene ambiance, making it an ideal spot for quiet reflection.\n\nBreathtaking Night Light Programs\n\nThe night light programs at Amar Jawan Jyoti are an absolute must-see. The stunning display of lights and animations brings the monument to life, showcasing the bravery and sacrifices of our soldiers in a unique and captivating way.\n\nA Tribute to Our Brave Soldiers\n\nThe monument's structure and animations provide a glimpse into the past, showcasing how wars were fought and the current state of our armed forces. The significance of the monument is sensitively conveyed, making it a truly unforgettable experience.\n\nVerdict\n\nAmar Jawan Jyoti is a must-visit destination in Jaipur.         "text": {
          "text": "A Gateway for the Commons:\n​Chand Pol, or the Moon Gate, is the main western entrance to the Amber Fort, a UNESCO World Heritage Site in Jaipur. While the royal family used the Sun Gate (Suraj Pol) to enter, the Chand Pol was the designated entry point for the common people, giving it a unique historical significance. Its name, \"Moon Gate,\" is thought to be derived from the direction it faces and its elegant design.\nArchitecturally, the gate showcases a beautiful fusion of Mughal and Rajput styles. It is a grand, multi-storied structure adorned with intricate carvings and traditional designs. The double-storied sections were likely used as a Naubat Khana, or drum house, where musicians would play music to announce important arrivals and mark different times of the day.\n​Despite being a functional entry for the general populace, its elaborate architecture proves that no detail was spared in its construction. The gate symbolizes the open nature of the fort, welcoming both the commoners and the royal court. It's a key feature that reflects the rich history and cultural heritage of Rajasthan, serving as an enduring link to the past.",

        "originalText": {
          "text": "A Gateway for the Commons:\n​Chand Pol, or the Moon Gate, is the main western entrance to the Amber Fort, a UNESCO World Heritage Site in Jaipur. While the royal family used the Sun Gate (Suraj Pol) to enter, the Chand Pol was the designated entry point for the common people, giving it a unique historical significance. Its name, \"Moon Gate,\" is thought to be derived from the direction it faces and its elegant design.\nArchitecturally, the gate showcases a beautiful fusion of Mughal and Rajput styles. It is a grand, multi-storied structure adorned with intricate carvings and traditional designs. The double-storied sections were likely used as a Naubat Khana, or drum house, where musicians would play music to announce important arrivals and mark different times of the day.\n​Despite being a functional entry for the general populace, its elaborate architecture proves that no detail was spared in its construction. The gate symbolizes the open nature of the fort, welcoming both the commoners and the royal court. It's a key feature that reflects the rich history and cultural heritage of Rajasthan, serving as an enduring link to the past.",
